2.3.11 Continued Consultation and Adaptive Management (VCS, 3.18; CCB, G3.4) 
With  reference  to  the  information  explained  in  section  2.3.520 information  sharing  meetings  with 
identified stakeholders and public consultation events are planned to be carried out at least once a 
year during the lifetime of this project. This will contribute to adaptive management of continued public 
consultations. 
2.3.12 Stakeholder Consultation Channels (CCB, G3.5) 
As explained in  this  PD,  no  communities  reside  within  the  project  area  or  its  immediate  borders. 
However,  communities  in  the  broader  project  zone  have  had  some  forms  of  involvement  in  illegal 
logging and deforestation activities in the project area due to economic pressures. 
 
With  the  project  implementation  halting  these  illegal  activities,  affected  individuals  will  have 
opportunities to engage in sustainable roles within the project. 
 
With  reference  to  section  2.3.3 of this  PD,  the  different  stakeholders  have  access  to  information 
relevant  to  each  stakeholder  group. This  project  prioritizes  community  participation  and  feedback. 
Local communities will lead the process of selecting their own representatives to engage in decision-
making from planning and implementation to monitoring. These representatives will work alongside 
regulatory  agencies  and  project  proponents  to  ensure  all  voices  are  heard  and  that  the  project's 
benefits  are  shared  equitably.  These  community  representative  will  cover  each  local  community  / 
villages. 
 
Public consultations with affected stakeholders have been conducted through several channels and 
will continue as needed, including: 
 
• Direct meetings with affected parties at designated locations 
• Distribution of questionnaires  
• Placement of 'suggestion boxes' in strategic locations, such as village offices, unit offices, and other 
frequented spots. 
2.3.13 Stakeholder Participation in Decision-Making and Implementation (VCS, 3.18, 3.19; 
CCB, G3.6) 
The  project  encompasses  both  internal  and  external  components.  Internal  components  include  the 
protection  of  the  project  area,  monitoring  its  impact,  and  restoration  efforts.  Although  there  are  no 
communities within  the  project  area  itself,  communities  located  in  the  surrounding  project  zone  are 
involved through various community development initiatives. There are communities residing in the 
broader   project   zone   from   where   some   representatives   have   been   involved   in   illegal 
logging/deforestation activities in the project area due to economic reasons. 
 
Since the project implementation will stop any such illegal activities and hence the livelihood for some 
in  those  communities,  the  affected  individuals  have  the  opportunity  to  be  involved  in  project 
implementation in a sustained basis. Related information is included in section 2.1.12 of this PD. 
 
Given the project's nature, intensive communication with the community is essential for its success. 
Stakeholders, particularly the community, play a crucial role in decision-making and implementation, 
as their interests are directly involved. 
 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
67 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.3 
The   public   consultations for   implementing   this   project   involved communicated   with several 
stakeholders  living  in  the  project  zone to  ensure  active  participation  in  decision-making, through 
several channels23 including the following, and will be repeated when required: 
 
• direct meeting with any affected parties at designated venues; 
 
• surveys using questioners. 
 
• announcements in the mass media or public facilities of villages, sub-districts; and 
 
• placing 'suggestion boxes' in strategic locations, for example: village offices, unit offices, or other 
locations frequented by the residents. 
 
Interventions  from  the  Sustainable  Commodities  Division  also  helped  to  bridge  the  communication 
between local communities in the surrounding area and PT. Kandelia Alam. How we engage them to 
explain that the project interventions will cover both carbon and non-carbon (beyond carbon) benefits, 
not  only  for  PT.  Kandelia  Alam  but  also  local  communities  through  several  programs  such  as; 
sustainable fisheries (mudcrab and croacker fish), research-based ecotourism and the development 
of sinking fund that will assist them in the replicability and scalability of the interventions. 
2.3.14 Anti-Discrimination Assurance (VCS 3.19; CCB, G3.7) 
To  ensure  that  all  entities  involved  in  the  project's  design  and  implementation  uphold  non-
discrimination  and  prevent  any  form  of harassment,  the  Board  of  Directors  has  issued  a  policy  on 
freedom   of   association   for   employees,   as   outlined   in   Company   Regulation   010/KLIA-ADM-
HRD/I/2021. This policy prohibits discrimination based on gender, race, religion, sexual orientation, or 
other characteristics. Additionally, the standard operating procedures detailed in Section 2.3.15 of this 
PD include a comprehensive stakeholder complaint and grievance resolution mechanism. This policy 
can be viewed by the VVB during validation processes. 
2.3.15 Feedback and Grievance Redress Procedure (VCS, 3.18.4; CCB, G3.8) 
The Project Proponents have developed a standard operating procedure (KLIA-PRO-4.1D-ED.01) for 
addressing any complaints and grievances. It allows any stakeholder to file a complaint against any 
party with the operational aspects of the project and the project area. The grievances will be handled 
by  using  cultural  and  social  approach  before  escalated  to  legal  formal  process.  The  grievances 
reporter will be treated respectfully and in confidence. 
 
Table 33: Feedback development and grievance redress procedure 
Development process The  project will  adopt  a  formal  grievance  and  redressal 
procedure to prevent and handle any conflicts with and among 
communities and other stakeholders that might arise during the 
implementation  of  project  activities. Necessary  ‘Standard 
Operating  Procedures  (“SOPs”) have  been  created  and 
socialized to internal teams and stakeholders. The steps to be 
applied in the complaint handling process flow is included below.

Grievance redress 
procedure 
• The Project Proponents have provided a complaint box both 
at the camp and at the village office. If any grievances occur 
and are reported from the project-zone communities and/or 
other  relevant  stakeholders  in  the  form  of  letters,  short 
messages  or  verbal  communication,  PT.  KLIA (Project 
Proponent) will  quickly  respond  to  them  by  following  the 
formal handling process. All reported cases will be assessed 
to  identify  and  verify  the  cause,  actors  and  scale  of 
grievances, and PT. KLIA verification team will recommend 
resolution  options  based  on  the  feedback  from  the 
stakeholders. The  degree  of  intervention  and  process  will 
depend on the nature of disputes, and PT. KLIA will continue 
to monitor the cases. 
• As  far  as  possible, conflicts  will  be resolved  through 
deliberation with mediation, and any legal process will be a 
last resort if no solution can be found. 
 
2.3.16 Accessibility of the Feedback and Grievance Redress Procedure (VCS, 3.19; CCB, 
G3.8) 
Any stakeholder with some grievance could approach designated ‘Person-In-Charge’ for specific types 
of complaints. The details are included in the standard operating procedures identified in section 2.3.12 
of this PD, and the channels of communication and accessibility are provided therein. 
 
The grievance procedure is designed to align with the principles of sustainable forest management, 
setting  out  the  criteria  designed  to  support  an  effective  non-judicial  grievance  mechanism.  The 
procedure includes aspects on legitimacy, accessibility, predictability, equity, transparency, conformity 
of rights, a source of continuous learning, and is based on engagement and dialogue. The procedure 
is  open  to  all  stakeholders,  although  it  is  primarily  focused  on  receiving  complaints  from  external 
sources, and for employees and local people with specific local level grievances.

2.3.18 Community Employment Opportunities (VCS, 3.19.13; CCB, G3.10) 
The project has a solid organizational structure and is equipped with clear job descriptions for each 
position. The project also has an equal opportunity recruitment procedure that is announced through 
social media and other media. Each position offered has requirements according to the job description 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
71 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.3 
and  does  not  discriminate  against  gender,  as  well  as  marginalized  people.  All  applicants  will  be 
selected through several stages, namely (1) the administrative stage which refers to the suitability of 
work experience and educational requirements with the job description. (2) the interview stage to find 
out more details of the files (curriculum vitae and/or resume) and knowledge of the job offered. (3) the 
psychological test stage to find out the applicant's personality. (4) the offering stage is the final stage 
which offers benefits to selected applicants according to the experience, knowledge, and grade of the 
position applied for.  
 
Besides the opportunity to work as a project employee, project has created sustainable and alternate 
employment opportunities for community members in the project zone who were earlier associated 
with illegal deforestation activities in the project area. These individuals can now be employed to assist 
with the implementation and operations of the project activities through the project lifetime that also 
enables them access to better health and working conditions. 
 
The Project Proponents have already initiated the processes and recruited several such individuals, 
and the scale of employment is planned to be increased as the scale of project activities increase over 
time. 
 
The Project  Proponent has  already  secured  agreement  from  Kubu  and  Batu Ampar  villages to 
implement some of the project plan such as supply of mangrove propagule, and supply of stake to 
support mangrove propagule. This is the actual employment opportunity from this project beside future 
benefit  for  the  community  from developing  community-led  business  model  generation  through 
cooperation on management and processing of kelulut honey, fisheries, mangrove-based ecotourism 
and education, and management of mangrove tea. 
2.3.19 Occupational Safety Assessment (VCS, 3.19; CCB, G3.12) 
The Project Proponent will adhere to the Safety and Health in Forestry Work guidelines published by 
the ILO, as well as comply with Law No. 13 of 2003 on Manpower, Law No. 1 of 1970 on Occupational 
Safety,  and  Law  No.  50  of  2012  on  the  implementation  of  the  Occupational  Health and  Safety 
Management System. 
 
An  occupational  safety  assessment  has  been  conducted  through  the  development  of  Hazard 
Identification,  Risk  Assessment,  and  Designated  Control  (HIRADC)  for  all  job  roles.  The Project 
Proponent will also provide first aid training, supply first aid kits to field employees, conduct medical 
check-ups,  and  provide  Personal  Protective  Equipment  (PPE)  in  accordance  with  the  HIRADC 
guidelines. 
 
Furthermore,  the Project Proponent will implement  an  occupational  health  and  safety management 
system  in  compliance  with  relevant  regulations,  ensuring  a  comprehensive  approach  to  employee 
health and safety within the company.

2.4.4 Project Management Partnerships and Team Development (VCS, 3.19; CCB, G4.2) 
The Project  Proponents have an in-house  team from  (i)  operation  and  site  management  team, (ii) 
impact and compliance team including thematic areas such as carbon, biodiversity, spatial and social, 
(iii) sustainable commodities team that will ensure the development of community-led business model 
as  well  as  supply  chain  and  value  chain  assistance  as  well  as,  (iv)  business  development  and 
innovative financing team for project implementation activities and uses any necessary support from 
regulatory agencies and external professionals to address all aspects of the project implementation 
needs.  For  operational  purposes,  if  any other support  will  be  required,  the Project  Proponents will 
procure such necessary services from suitable entities.

2.4.6 Avoidance of Corruption and Other Unethical Behavior (VCS, 3.19; CCB, G4.3) 
The Project Proponents have established and documented a strict policy to  prevent corruption and 
other unethical behavior, ensuring compliance with third-party grant requirements for project initiation. 
This  policy  will  be  upheld  throughout  the  project's  duration (refer to Project  Proponent’s, i.e., PT 
Kandelia Alam, policy on Avoidance of Corruption and Other Unethical Behavior). 
2.4.7 Commercially Sensitive Information (VCS, 3.5.2 – 3.5.4; CCB Rules, 3.5.13 – 3.5.14)  
The following information has been deemed by the Project Proponents to be commercially sensitive 
and will be discussed and explained with the VVB during the validation processes. 
 
1. Capital and operations expenses, including salaries paid to employees. 
2. Contracts and agreements among the parties involved in the project. 
3. Financial projection - Detailed 30-year financial projection for the project which includes all 
project-related costs and ex-ante carbon estimates. 
4. Electronic form files of project area, proxy area, and buffer zone - GIS boundary shape files 
are used to describe the project area and buffer zone. 
5. All agreements between Project Proponents and other related partners governing the 
implementation of project activities: Agreements between technical partners, communities and 
government. 
6. The model used to make carbon calculations - The computer model generates carbon 
estimates from all field and remote sensing data. 
7. Project budget and workplan - Detailed implementation of workplan.

2.5.3 Human Rights (VCS, 3.19)  
The project area is privately owned with concessions granted to private entities who are the Project 
Proponents for  sustainable  eco-system  management.  There  were  and  currently  no  populations 
inhabiting the project area and its immediate surroundings. There is no customary right holders and 
indigenous and tribal communities. Hence, ILO Convention 169
24
 provisions are not applicable to this 
project activity. 
 
 
24
 ILO Convention 169 recognizes Indigenous peoples' right to self-determination within a nation-state, while setting standards for 
national governments regarding Indigenous peoples' economic, socio-cultural and political rights, including the right to a land base.

2.5.4 Indigenous Peoples and Cultural Heritage (VCS, 3.18, 3.19) 
Based on the results of an HCV assessment conducted in 2013 by the previous owners of the project 
area, the Project Proponents have identified HCV 5 and HCV 6 areas within the project boundary and 
in the  project  zone.  This  identification is  used  as  a  primary  information  source  for the  HCV 
management plan to ensure protection for these sites with social and cultural value to the community 
and are appropriately conserved in the project. 
 
2.5.5 Statutory and Customary Property Rights (VCS, 3.18, 3.19; CCB, G5.1) 
The  project area is  classified  as  forest  area  under  the  authority  of  Ministry  of  Environment  and 
Forestry.  The  ministry  has  assigned  the  project  area  to  PT.  Kandelia  Alam,  based  on  Ministry  of 
Forestry Decree No. SK.249/MENHUT-II/2008 dated 24 June 2008 concerning Issuance of Natural 
Forest Concession (IUOPHHK-HA) for PT. Kandelia Alam on Production Forest for total area of 18,130 
ha. The Ministry of Environment and Forestry then issued decree No. 
S.295/MENLHK/SETJEN/HPL.1/2023 concerning Work Area Designation for total area of 18,041.62 
hectares dated 31 March 2023. The description of the land cover of the area is presented in section 
2.1.5 of this PD. 
 
There are three villages within the project zone, which are Kubu village, and Batu Ampar villages, and 
no settlements or residency are located within the project area. Some of the villagers illegally collect 
and harvest firewood from the project area for use as firewood in the coconut sugar industry in the 
surrounding areas. The map of the village and their cultivation area is available in section 2.1.6.  
 
No statutory and customary property rights were identified with respect to the project area for which 
the Project Proponents have project activity license. 
 
2.5.6 Recognition of Property Rights (VCS, 3.7, 3.18, 3.19; CCB, G5.1) 
Though  no  statutory  and  customary  property  rights  were  identified  within  the  project  area  for  any 
communities,  the Project  Proponents are  committed  to  recognizing,  respecting,  and  supporting  all 
property rights of communities and other stakeholders outside the project area and in the project zone 
for communities living in the four villages.

2.5.8 Benefit Sharing Mechanisms (VCS, 3.18, 3.19;) 
 
Table 40: Details for Benefit Sharing Mechanism 
 
Process used 
to design the 
benefit sharing 
plan  
Baseline  studies and  a series  of  focus group  discussions  have  been 
carried  out  in  the  project  zone;  activities  carried  out  together  with 
community groups to build a sustainable business model for improving 
livelihoods. Together with village officials, we also develop ‘community 
partnership’ programs,  especially  in  terms  of  education,  health,  and 
improving facilities and infrastructure in affected villages. 
Summary of 
the benefit 
sharing plan 
The results of the baseline study and focus group discussions agreed on 
several  sustainable  livelihood  business  models, such  as, (1) farmer 
group participation in land rehabilitation effort through the KBR (Kebun 
Bibit Rakyat) program, (2) pilot project for mangrove crab cultivation, (3) 
horticultural  cultivation  to  support  vegetable  needs  in  the camp, (4) 
collection  and  development  of ‘non  timber  forest  products  (“NTFP”)’ 
products (honey and mangrove tea), (5) the development of research-
based ecotourism to provide on the ground experience for early stage 
researcher  globally  but  also  provide  exposure  to  PT.  Kandelia Alam 
employees and local communities on the importance of the mangrove 
ecosystem. 
Approval and 
dissemination 
of benefit 
sharing plan 
In June 2024 two MOUs were agreed on for mangrove plant nurseries 
and horticulture/vegetable cultivation. The signing of the agreement was 
attended and received support from the village government. Meanwhile, 
for the other two programs, pilot studies are currently being carried out 
by inviting experts in collaboration with universities around the camp. 
The community partnership program has been implemented since last 
year in the form of support for educational scholarships and assistance 
for school facilities and infrastructure (boats) as well as assistance for 
commemorating religious holidays. 
2.5.9 Property Rights Protection (VCS, 3.18, 3.19; CCB, G5.3) 
This project does not have any plan to remove or relocate property rights holders from their lands or 
territories, since there is no community living inside the project area. 
 
2.5.10 Illegal Activity Identification (VCS, 3.19; CCB, G5.4) 
Illegal logging has been a recurring issue in the project area, often carried out by certain community 
members primarily  from  Kubu  and  Batu Ampar  villages.  This  activity  is  driven  by  the  need  for 
mangrove timber, used for fuel in raw sugar production and as raw material for mangrove charcoal. 
Additionally, residents of Kubu village continue to engage in mangrove charcoal production through 
burning processes, with approximately 500 ovens in Batu Ampar village and 20 stoves in Kubu village 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
86 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.3 
identified. Mangrove  wood  that  is  used  as the  main  raw  material  for  making  mangrove  charcoal  is 
identified to have high commercial value in the illegal timber market. 
 
Kubu village is home to 257 fishermen, while Batu Ampar village has 356 fishermen. Unfortunately, 
some fishermen in these communities employ destructive methods such as explosives and electricity. 
 
Project proponent ensures does not and will not use victims of human trafficking, forced labor, and 
child labor by referring to Law no. 13/2023 concerning employment and Law no. 11/2020 concerning 
job creation. 
 
To address these issues, the project aims to develop alternative sustainable livelihoods, as outlined 
in section 2.1.18. 
 
 
Charcoal activities in Batu Ampar Village 
2.5.11 Ongoing Disputes (VCS, 3.18, 3.19; CCB, G5.5) 
There is no ongoing dispute with any parties in relation to the project area and project activities.

2.6 Additional Information Relevant to the Project  
2.6.1 Leakage Management (VCS, 3.11, 3.15) 
Based on leakage assessment by the Project Proponents, it is concluded that there will be no 
leakage resulting from implementation of the project activities. Justification for this conclusion with 
reference to the applied VCS methodologies is explained below for each type of project activity; 
further explanation is included in section 3.2.3 of this PD. 
 
1. For the IFM project activity implementation, there will be no source of leakage emissions due to 
the following reasons: 
• there is no activity shifting leakage, as there is no intensification operations for selective 
logging nor shifted operations for selective logging to areas outside of the project boundary 
that is more than harvesting activities planned in the baseline scenario based on business 
license, and 
• there is no market leakage, as there is intensification of existing harvest practices, nor 
formation of new enterprise for sanctioned selective logging to replace the activities in the 
baseline scenario. 
 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
89 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.3 
2. For the ARR project activity, the procedure for quantification of leakage emission uses several 
sources  of  framework,  such  as  AR-TOOL  15  and  AR-ACM0003.  Based  on  AR-TOOL  15 
document, leakage emission attributable to the displacement of agricultural activities due to 
implementation of an A/R CDM project activity is estimated as the decrease in carbon stocks in 
the affected carbon pools of the land receiving the displaced activity. In this project, leakage 
emission  attributable  to  the  displacement  of  grazing activities  are  not  relevant  and  hence 
accounted as zero. 
 
3. For the REDD and WRC project activities, according to module VMD0009-LK-ASP, the value 
ΔC_(LK-AS, planned)  is  considered  to  be  zero  since  the Project  Proponent will  not  either 
designate new lands as timber concessions, increase harvest rates in lands already managed 
for timber, clear intact forests for agricultural production, or increase fertilizer use to enhance 
agricultural yield. Hence, there will be no leakage emissions from the REDD component of this 
project. 
 
Therefore, no leakage management is planned for this project. 
 
2.6.2 Further Information  
Except for those identified in other sections in this PD, no other legislative, technical, economic, 
sectoral, social, environmental, geographic, site-specific and/or temporal information are relevant.

3 CLIMATE 
3.1 Application of Methodology 
3.1.1 Title and Reference of Methodology (VCS, 3.1) 
The selection and application of the relevant VCS methodologies followed a three-step approach 
explained below: 
 
Step 1. Identification  of pre-project  conditions  prior  to  implementation  of  the WRC eco-system 
conservation project and its component activities that result in climate benefits in above-ground and 
below-ground carbon pools; 
 
Step 2. Identification of eligible types of VCS project activities with reference to Table 4 in Appendix 
1 of VCS Standards (version 4.7) for the pre-project and project conditions as per Step 1; and 
 
Step 3. Identification of VCS methodologies that apply to eligible project types as per Step 3. 
 
 
 
The most recent versions of the applied VCS methodologies and associated tools are identified in 
Table 42 and Table 43 below. However, it should be noted that if any of the methodology or tool gets 
updated  during  any  time  until  the  final  version  of  this  PD  at  VCS  registration,  irrespective  of 
whichever version is mentioned in the PD, the applicable version will be the most recent applicable 
version approved by Verra.

3.1.3 Project Boundary (VCS, 3.12) 
As explained in section 2.1.1. of this PD, the project activities are of the following four types individually 
covering the area sizes identified below out of a total area of 18,041.62 ha (also refer section 2.1.14 
of this PD): 
 
• IFM+CIW type: 15,004.05 hectares 
• RWE+ARR type: 464 hectares, and 
• REDD+CIW type (for AUDD): 1,266.71 hectares 
• CIW (Stand-alone): 161 hectares. 
 
 
Each of the above three types of project activities are planned in certain pre-identified areas within the 
overall  project  area  based  on  the  nature  of  pre-project scenarios  and activities occurring  in 
corresponding areas, and likely scenarios in the absence the planned/approved future activities (also 
refer  Section  2.1.17 and Figure 8 for  Theory  of  Change)  and  as  per  requirements  in  the  business 
license (or, RKU). The sources of baseline emissions and project emissions are, therefore, explained 
below separately for each of the three types of project activities.

3.1.4 Baseline Scenario (VCS, 3.13) 
The baseline scenarios for each of the three components in the project are explained below. 
 
IFM+CIW Component: Baseline Scenario as per VM0011 and VM0007 
 
Step 1: In the absence of the VCS IFM+CIW project, the realistic and credible alternative baseline 
scenarios available to the Project Proponents are: (1) either continue with timber harvesting for 
commercial purposes with reference to its business license that is valid from 2008 to 2053, or (2) 
implement  the  IFM  project  without  VCS  registration  using  an  eco-system  conservation  and 
restoration  license  to  replace  the  timber  harvesting license.  Being  licensed  activities,  both 
alternatives are enforceable mandatorily by the Indonesian regulations. 
 
Step 2: Of these two alternative baseline scenarios, both were possible to be implemented with 
skills and expertise available with the Project Proponents. However, the second alternative faces 
significant  financial  barriers  because  it  doesn’t  and  cannot  generate  revenues  with  eco-system 
restoration activities needed for sustaining capital to implement and operate and maintain it. 
 
Therefore, this alternative baseline scenario is eliminated from further consideration, and the first 
baseline alternative is determined to be the baseline scenario for the IFM+CIW component of this 
project. 
 
The baseline scenario for the IFM+CIW component will be re-assessed every 10 years and updated 
as necessary
28
  as per with the logging permit planning regulations in Indonesia. In the ex-ante 
assessment, the assumption is that the baseline scenario for this component will continue into the 
2032 period and beyond, following a harvesting cycle every 20 years as per the harvesting business 
plan that was previously approved by the relevant Indonesian government agency. 
 
RWE+ARR Component: Baseline Scenario as per VM0007 and T-ADD 
 
With reference to Table 2 of VM0007 (Determining RWE+ARR suitability), the land on which the 
RWE+ARR component is implemented comprises degraded land and unmanaged forest in tidal 
wetland and therefore is suitable for implementation of RWE+ARR activities. 
 
 
28
 Refer 4.2.5 of VCS Standard (version 4.7 dated 4 October 2023). 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
104 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.3 
Step 1: The possible alternatives to implementation of the RWE+ARR activities are: (1) continuation 
of the pre-project land use which is not undertaking any re-planting activities and allowing the land 
to  continue  to  remain  in  pre-project  conditions  that  may  lead  to  further  degradation,  and  (2) 
implement the RWE+ARR project consisting replanting in degraded and open areas but without VCS 
registration using an eco-system conservation and restoration license. Either of these alternatives 
could have been implemented as both alternative scenarios are covered by respective licenses as 
per Indonesian regulations. 
 
Step 2: Alternative scenario 1 would result in possible expansion of degradation and gradual loss of 
carbon stock in the unmanaged forests and already degraded and deforested areas as there is no 
incentive for the Project Proponents to implement the RWE+ARR activities within their overall project 
boundary.  On  the  other  hand,  if  the Project  Proponents undertook  alternative  scenario  2  and 
implemented RWE+ARR activities that was requirement for investments including for sustenance 
costs. 
 
Therefore,  alternative  scenario  2  is  unlikely  to  be  undertaken  and  is  eliminated  from  further 
consideration,  and  alternative  scenario  1  is  determined  to  be  the  baseline  scenario  for  the 
RWE+ARR component of this project. 
 
The baseline scenario for the RWE+ARR component will be re-assessed every 10 years and revised 
as necessary, based on the same provisions in the VCS Standard discussed elsewhere in this PD 
for the IFM and REDD components of this project. 
 
REDD+CIW Component: Baseline Scenario as per VM0007 and T-ADD 
 
With reference to Table 1 of VM0007 (Decision Tree for Determining REDD Project Activity Type), 
the land on which the REDD component is implemented is not legally authorized to be converted to 
non-forest or managed tree plantation and is designated for protection/conservation as per both the 
previous business license and the current replacement license. However, illegal logging has taken 
place in this part of the project area in patterns resembling unplanned deforestation. Therefore, the 
conservation  activities  being  implemented  in  this  part  of  the  project  area  constitutes  ‘avoided 
unplanned deforestation and degradation (“AUDD”)’ type of REDD project activity. This area is also 
an intact tidal wetland facing deforestation/forest degradation of unplanned type from agents/drivers 
of  such as  described  earlier.  Therefore,  the conservation  activities  being  implemented  can  be 
categorized as ‘Conservation of Intact wetland (“CIW”)’ type of REDD activities with reference to 
Table 3 of VM0007. 
 
Step 1: The possible alternatives to implementation of the REDD activities are: (1) continuation of 
the pre-project land use which is unchecked deforestation and forest degradation by agents/drivers 
of deforestation that is illegal logging and associated forest clearance activities within the overall 
project area in the concession that is forested but not designated for commercial timbering, and (2) 
implement  the  REDD  project  without  VCS  registration  using  an  eco-system  conservation  and 
restoration  license. Both  of  these  could  go  on  as  both  alternative  scenarios  are  covered  by 
respective licenses as per Indonesian regulations. 
 
Step 2: Alternative scenario 1 would result in unplanned deforestation and degradation in the intact 
wetland that is part of the overall timbering concession license but there is no incentive for the 
Project  Proponents to  enforce  conservation  measures.  However,  the Project  Proponents could 
undertake alternative scenario 2 and implement conservation activities that require investments and 
sustenance costs but still no incentives. 
 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
105 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.3 
Therefore,  alternative  scenario  2  is  unlikely  to  be  undertaken  and  is  eliminated  from  further 
consideration, and alternative scenario 1 is determined to be the baseline scenario for the AUPD-
REDD (CIW-REDD) component. 
 
The baseline scenario for the REDD component will be re-assessed every 10 years and revised as 
necessary, based on same provisions in the VCS Standard mentioned earlier for IFM component of 
this projects. 
3.1.5 Additionality (VCS, 3.14) 
Though different in terms of respective pre-project and baseline scenarios, the three components of 
the project activities in this VCS project are simultaneously implemented within the same project 
boundary on  a  combined  basis  with  reference  to  the  same  approval  license  on  eco-system 
conservation. Due to conceptual and structural similarities in the steps to demonstrate additionality 
as described in the above three VCS guidelines, the additionality demonstration for the proposed 
VCS project and its three components are explained below in a consolidated but component-specific 
basis. The additionality methods are explained in 3.1.5.2 of this PD. 
 
The implementation of none of these project activities was mandated in Indonesian law but was 
specifically  applied  for  and  approval  obtained  by  the Project  Proponents. The  additional  GHG 
emission reductions that the implementation of these project activities will result in compared to the 
pre-project and baseline scenario is explained applying the following three VCS guidelines: 
 
• VT001 (Version 3.0): Tool for the demonstration of additionality in VCS Agriculture, Forestry and 
Other Land Use (AFOLU) project activities as required in VM0011 (version 1.0), 
 
• T-ADD: Combined tool to identify the baseline scenario and demonstrate additionality in A/R 
CDM project activities as required in VM0007 (version 1.7), and 
 
• VMD0052: Demonstration of additionality of tidal wetland restoration and conservation project 
activities, as per the VCS Program requirements.

3.1.5.2 Additionality Methods (VCS, 3.14) 
The following steps have been applied for additionality demonstration as per VT001 (Version 3.0) 
and in VM0007 (version 1.7). 
 
STEP 1. Identification of alternative land use scenarios to the AFOLU project activity 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
106 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.3 
 
IFM+CIW component of the VCS project. With reference to the requirements in sub-steps 1(a), 1(b) 
and 1(c) of VT001 (Version 3.0), three plausible and credible alternative land use scenarios involving 
trees/vegetation available in the project area were assessed to select the baseline scenario for the 
IFM+CIW component. These three alternatives are: 
 
1. Continuation  with  pre-project  land  use  which  is  timber  harvesting  for  commercial  exploitation  of 
available trees as per the concession license awarded to PT Kandelia Alam in 2008, 
 
2. Without applying  for  VCS  registration,  replace  the  concession  license  and  instead  secure  new 
license to implement conservation of the intact areas previously approved for logging and any that 
has already been logged so as to prevent further degradation, and 
 
3. a combination of 1 and 2 above, which is part of the concession area to be commercially harvested, 
and the balance area conserved without applying this latter part of the concession area included in 
any application for VCS registration. 
 
While all three alternatives are credible and permitted under the Indonesian laws, and the Project 
Proponent could choose any of these. 
 
However, while the first and the third alternatives would provide commercial incentives to the Project 
Proponent, the second alternative does not provide any incentive and cannot be sustained without 
any financial support. 
 
Between alternatives one and three, it would have been operationally challenging to delineate which 
portion  of  the  project  area  could  be  cost  effectively  conserved  or  commercially  harvested,  and 
continuously monitored throughout the lifetime of the conservation project to prevent secondary 
degradation. 
 
Hence, alternative 1 is selected as the baseline scenario that would have occurred if no IFM activities 
were implemented. A barrier analysis is performed in STEP 3 below to assess if the IFM activities in 
place of approved logging activities face more barriers that may prevent their implementation. 
 
RWE+ARR  component  of  the  VCS  project.  With  respect  to  sub-step  (0)  of  T-ADD,  it  can  be 
confirmed by the Project Proponents that this ARR component of the VCS project started after 1 
January 2022. The decision was based on corporate commitment by PT Kandelia Alam in relation 
to  which  it  has  obtained  necessary  licenses  from  the  Ministry  of  Environment  and  Forestry  in 
Indonesia. 
 
With reference to the requirements in sub-steps 1(a) and 1(b) of T-ADD, there could be two realistic 
and credible land-use scenarios that would have occurred on the land identified for ARR activities 
within the overall project boundary for this VCS project. These three alternatives are: 
 
1. Continuation with pre-project land-use which is allowing the land to lie vacant without any economic 
use  or  exploitation  and  gradually  degrade  over  time,  irrespective  of  any  other  types  of  activities 
implemented in other parts with the overall project boundary for the VCS project, and 
 
2. Implementation of RWE+ARR activities without applying for VCS registration. 
 
While  both  alternatives  are  credible  and  permitted  under  the  Indonesian  laws,  and  the Project 
Proponent could have chosen any of these. 
 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
107 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.3 
The second alternative does not provide any incentive to the Project Proponent and cannot be 
sustained without any financial support, and it is certain that in the absence of the ARR activities, 
the open areas as well as the areas that were previously deforested would be further degraded. 
 
Hence, alternative one is selected as the baseline scenario. A barrier analysis is performed in STEP 
3  below  to  assess  if  the RWE+ARR  activities  face  more barriers that  may  prevent  their 
implementation. 
 
REDD component of the VCS project. The trees/vegetation available in the project area are: either 
(1) not selected/included in approved business plan for commercial harvesting, or (2) will not be 
harvested at all during the 10-year approved harvesting cycle (as in IFM) and will continue to be not 
harvested after this period. Based on evidence available with the Project Proponent including photos 
and video recordings for the project area, wide-spread levels of unplanned and illegal logging have 
been observed in all these areas, that the proposed REDD component of this project is planned to 
prevent. 
 
Therefore, with reference to the requirements in sub-steps 1(a), 1(b) and 1(c) of VT001 (Version 3.0), 
the following two plausible and credible alternative land use scenarios are identified: 
 
1. Continuation  with  pre-project  land  use  with  no intervention  to  prevent  illegal  deforestation  and 
degradation, irrespective of any other types of activities implemented in other parts with the overall 
project boundary for the VCS project, and 
 
2. Without applying for VCS registration, implement REDD activities that will result in prevention of 
the illegal logging activities. 
 
Both alternatives are credible, and the Indonesian laws do not require the Project Proponents to be 
involved in any of these. The Project Proponents could have continued without implementing any 
REDD activity. Also, the second alternative does not provide any incentive to the Project Proponent 
and cannot be sustained without any financial support, and it is certain that the pre-project conditions 
are likely to continue and increase without any intervention. 
 
Hence, alternative 1 is selected as the baseline scenario that would have occurred if no REDD 
activities were implemented. A barrier analysis is performed in STEP 3 below to assess if the REDD 
activities  in  Alternative  2  to  prevent  illegal  logging  face  more  barriers  that  may  prevent  their 
implementation. 
 
Based on conclusions from STEP 1 above, for each of the three VCS project components, IFM, ARR 
and REDD, a combined barrier analysis is performed in STEP 3. 
 
STEP 3. Barrier Analysis 
 
Investment  barrier: The Project Proponents,  who  are  private  entities,  decided  to  discontinue 
harvesting activities that generated commercial benefits. Instead, they decided to implement various 
types of project activities to conserve native forestry assets and regenerate and revegetate areas that 
are  degraded  or  under  degradation.  No  of  the  VCS  project  activity  components  generate  any 
commercial benefits, though these are required to be sustained in the longer term (as discussed under 
‘Theory of Change’). 
 
Being private entities, it is not easy to access sustained funding to implement and continue the VCS 
project activities through at least the project life. 
 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
108 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.3 
Debt funding is rare even in the presence of approval by the relevant Indonesian government agencies 
to  implement  a  conservation  project.  At  the  same  time  the  project  did  not  have  access  to  any 
international or domestic funding to sustain it. Hence, the project is planned and is being implemented 
with shareholders equity. 
 
Possibility  of  any  additional  funding  could  be  based  on  potential  registration  as  a  VCS  project. 
However, when the Project Proponents conceptualized the conservation project on 1 August 2021 and 
decided  not  to  continue  with  timber  harvesting,  the  rules  of  carbon  credits  under  the  Indonesian 
regulations were not clear or available. At that time the market risks were perceived to be very high. 
 
Such investment barriers are not expected in any of the baseline scenarios in any of the three types 
of project components. 
 
Institutional barriers: As mentioned above, from a regulatory context, at the time of conceptualizing 
and  subsequently  initiating  the  proposed  VCS  project,  the  Indonesian  regulations  governing  the 
monetization  of  carbon  credits  from AFOLU  sector amongst  others were in  development.  Hence,  it 
was not clear how the expected final regulations would affect the proposed VCS project. 
 
As  a  result,  the  implementation  of  this  VCS  project  faced  institutional  barriers  due  io  regulatory 
uncertainties. 
 
Based on the investment and institutional barriers that this VCS project faces that are not faced in the 
baseline scenarios, it is not business-as-usual for the Project Proponents to implement it. Based on 
this conclusion from barrier analysis, a common practice analysis is performed below in STEP 4 with 
reference to the additionality guidelines referred above. 
 
STEP 4. Common Practice Analysis 
 
For each of the three types of project components (IFM, REDD and ARR) analyzed above, it is evident 
that  the  respective  component  is  more  difficult  to  implement  and  faces  distinct  barriers  to 
implementation and sustenance. In addition, it is clear by referring to published information by Verra 
and other frameworks about AFOLU projects that this is the only and a unique project in Indonesia 
that is a combination of three distinct components collated within a common project boundary linked 
by a common eco-system restoration license in an inland wetland area. Therefore, it is not common 
to Indonesia in several respects. 
 
Based on the above, additionality is clearly demonstrated for all three components and project 
types implemented for IFM+CIW, RWE+ARR and REDD. Therefore, the project is additional. 
 
3.1.6 Methodology Deviations (VCS, 3.20) 
The application of two methodologies to the three components in this project required certain essential 
deviations  to  ensure  conservativeness  of  the  GHG  reduction  estimates.  These  deviations  relate  to 
assessment of project emissions. Since the three components of the project are required to employ 
common resources and infrastructure, such as use of boats to patrol the entire project area, the project 
emissions that will result from such common activities are estimated on a combined basis to represent 
the actuals (refer section 3.2.2 of this PD). The procedures will be explained to the VVB during the 
validation processes.

CCB v3.0, VCS v4.3 
3.2 Quantification of Estimated GHG Emission Reductions and Removals 
3.2.1 Baseline Emissions (VCS, 3.15) 
The baseline emissions in relation to the three types of project activities (IFM, ARR and REDD) in this 
VCS project are explained below in the following sub-sections of section 3.2.1. 
 
IMPROVED FOREST Management (IFM) 
The procedure of quantification of baseline emissions and/or removals is as per VM0011 IFM-LtPF 
(Improved Forest Management – Logged to Protected Forest) Version 1.0 Sectoral Scope 14 which 
provides a procedure for determining the net anthropogenic GHG emission reduction associated with 
an  IFM-LtPF  activity  which  prevents  the  degradation  of  a  forest  through  the  shifting  of  a  baseline 
activity of selective logging to conservation. This procedure for the baseline emission identification and 
estimation involves the following: 
 
1. primary parameters in the project area  
2. baseline emissions from degradation  
3. baseline activity emissions. 
 
1. Calculation of primary parameters in the project area 
The primary parameters are collected for the second option out of the three provided in VM0011. This 
option (refer figure below for dotted red line) is based on existing inventory data collected by the Project 
Proponent involving a ‘More Detailed Forest Inventory Report (“FIR”)’ it has prepared by undertaking 
primary field data gathering exercise necessary for this option. The use of any secondary data and 
references where necessary involved those that are applicable to Indonesia. 
 
Figure 15: Schematic of data sources required for IFM-LtPF methodology29 
 
The FIR prepared for this project is the IKHB report that also is required by the relevant Indonesian 
authorities for the purposes of various approvals necessary for implementing this project. 
 
The inputs parameters for application of an ‘Allometric Method’ in relation to the FIR approach are: 
 
• tree species and wood density, separately for ‘Mangrove Forest stratum’ and ‘Swamp Forest 
stratum’ which are the two dominant and distinct eco-systems in the project area 
 
29
 Source: Figure 1-1 and Figure 3-1 in VM0011 Version 1.0

CCB v3.0, VCS v4.3 
 
• DBH of trees from both forest strata using a method of sampling plots 
 
• carbon stock in AGB and BGB for both forest strata using allometric method, and in Soil Organic 
Carbon, and 
 
• annual  volume  of  merchantable  timber  potential  both  forest  strata  with  reference  to  previously 
approved business plan for timber harvesting. 
 
The  various  equations  that  were  used  to  estimate  the  total  emissions  in  the  baseline  scenario  are 
listed  below  in  the  sequence  of  completing  the  estimates.  The  keys  aspects  of  the  estimations 
completed are explained with formulas that are applied to complete the estimates.

of IFM-LtPF.

a. Carbon  in  Deadwood  from 'Damaged  and  Leftover  AGB'  of  various  types  due  to logging 
activities (3.3.1 of VM0011) 
As  a result of  selective  logging  that  would  have  occurred  in  the  baseline  scenario,  the  trimmed 
branches, bark, and foliage of the logged trees would have been left on the forest floor contributing to 
the ‘deadwood (“DW”)’ pool, and slowly decaying over time. DW could  comprise  carbon  in  coarse 
woody  debris,  standing  dead  trees  and  other  dead  material  not  included  in  the  litter  or  soil  carbon 
pools (refer IPCC 2006, p4.73). In addition, trees that could get damaged during the logging operations 
are considered as ‘Residual Stand Damage (“RSD”)’ and are also included as carbon input to the DW 
pool. These two DW components (also referred to as inputs) contributing to the carbon in the DW pool 
are explained below. 
 
i. Carbon from residual stand damage (퐶
푅푆퐷,푡

3. Calculation for total baseline activity emissions 
Several sources of carbon emissions are relevant in the timber harvesting activities in the baseline in 
the  absence  of  IFM  project  activity.  These  are  identified  below  as  per  the  generalized  schematic 
reproduced  from  VM0011  for  the  different  stages  of  timber  harvesting  operations  (refer  Figure 16 
included below). 
 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
121 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.3 
 
 
Figure 16: Outline of timber harvesting operations and associated emission sources
31
 
 
In  this  IFM  project,  the  baseline  emissions  from  use  of  energy  sources  in  the  following  operational 
activities for use of fossil fuels (diesel) have been obtained by the Project Proponent (current owner 
of  the  project  area)  from  the  previous  owners.  These  relate  to  harvesting  and  transportation  of 
harvested timber to barges for dispatching to customers, as listed below: 
 
• Fuel Consumption of Equipment for felling and snigging of merchantable log, 
• Fuel Consumption of Equipment for hauling, and 
• Fuel Consumption for transport of harvested logs to mother vessel for export. 
 
Due to lack of other types of operational data that contributes to in the baseline emissions for other 
activities identified in Figure 9, such emissions have been excluded conservatively. 
 
No electricity consumption from the electricity grid is relevant in the baseline for the IFM component. 
 
Any project emissions resulting from fossil fuel use during operation of the IFM project activities will 
be monitored ex post and included in each monitoring report. 
 
To  calculate GHG  emissions due  to  harvesting  activities  that  involve  fossil  fuel  (diesel)  use  for 
merchantable logging, the following equation is applied (refer VM0011).

The transportation related GHG emissions in the baseline are to be estimated, as per Equation 3-44, 
Equation 3-45 and Equation 3-46, and Equation 3-51, Equation 3-52, Equation 3-53, and Equation 3-
54  of  VM0011.  All  necessary input  parameters for applying  these  formulae are not  available  to  the 
Project  Proponent (i.e.,  the  current  owner  of  the  Project  Area).  However,  it  was  possible  to  obtain 
records for fossil fuel (diesel) used by the previous owners of the Project Area for transportation and 
distribution (2-way  transport)  of  harvested  logs  from  the  Project  Area  by  water  transport  (smaller 
barges)  to  a  mother  vessel  in  deeper  waterbody.  Hence,  the  GHG  emission  estimation  for  these 
components in the baseline are modified as below, whereby providing a conservative baseline GHG 
emissions estimation.

AFFORESTATION, REFORESTATION, AND REVEGETATION (ARR) 
The procedure  of  quantification  of  baseline  removals  with  carbon  stock  changes  that  would  have 
occurred  in  the  absence  of  the  activities  involving  the  ARR  project  component  is  selected  with 
reference to the decision tree provided in Table 2 of VM0007 (v1.8) and considered in combination 
with VM0047 (v1.0). 
 
The  procedure  of  quantification  of  baseline  emissions  and/or  removals uses the VM0047 as  the 
primary  base  that  refers  to  other  procedures  such  as  AR-ACM0003  for  different  parts  of  the 
calculations applying a census-based approach. 
 
Formulae/equations provided in the above identified methodology and its applicable tools are applied 
in the sequence included below for completing the GHG estimates for ARR component of this project. 
The  keys  aspects  of  the  estimations  completed  are  explained  with formulas that  are  applied  to 
complete the estimates. 
 
Net GHG removals in the ARR baseline scenario 
The  following  sections/provisions  are  applicable  though  these  are  not  applied  ex  ante  and  are 
conservatively excluded; these could be included optionally as part of ex post monitoring: 
 
• Paragraph 11 and paragraph 12(g) of AR-TOOL14 (v04.2) 
• Paragraphs 33, 34, 35 and 8.1 (Table 5.) of AR-TOOL12 (v03.1), and Paragraph 9 (Table 1.) of

• Equation (1) of BL-ARR.

In calculating Net GHG removal in the baseline ARR scenario, following sub-components are identified 
for applying in the ex-ante scenario. 
 
• According to AR-TOOL14 version 04.2 regarding methodological tool – estimation of carbon stocks 
and change in carbon stocks of trees and shrubs in A/R CDM project activities, there are several 
conditions under which carbon stock and change in carbon stock may be estimated as zero, which 
are:  
• Carbon stock in trees in the baseline can be accounted as zero if all of the following conditions are 
met: 
• the  pre-project  trees  are  neither  harvested,  nor  cleared,  nor  removed  throughout  the  crediting 
period of the project activity; 
• the pre-project trees do not suffer mortality because of competition from trees planted in the project, 
or damage because of implementation of the project activity, at any time during the crediting period 
of the project activity; 
• the pre-project trees are not inventoried along with the project trees in monitoring of carbon stocks 
but their continued existence, consistent with the baseline scenario, is monitored throughout the 
crediting period of the project activity. 
• Changes in carbon stocks in trees and shrubs in the baseline can be accounted as zero for those 
lands for which the Project Proponents can demonstrate through documentary evidence or through 
participatory rural appraisal (PRA) that one or more of the following indicators apply: 
• observed  reduction  in  topsoil  depth  (e.g.,  as  shown  by  root  exposure,  presence  of  pedestals, 
exposed sub-soil horizons); 
• presence of gully, sheet or rill erosion; or landslides, or other forms of mass-movement erosion; 
• presence of plant species locally known to be indicators of infertile land; 
• land comprises of bare sand dunes, or other bare lands; 
• land contains contaminated soils, mine spoils, or highly alkaline or saline soils; 
• land is subjected to periodic cycles (e.g., slash-and-burn, or clearing-regrowing cycles) so that the 
biomass oscillates between a minimum and a maximum value in the baseline; and 
• other project specific conditions discussed earlier. 
 
• According to AR-ACM0003 version 02.0 sectoral scope 14 regarding A/R Large-scale Consolidated 
Methodology – Afforestation and reforestation of lands except wetlands, in section for baseline and 
monitoring  methodology  for  selection  of  carbon  pools  and  greenhouse  gases  accounted,  the 
following carbon pools are accounted for carbon stock changes.

REDUCING EMISSIONS FROM DEFORESTATION AND DEGRADATION (REDD) 
The procedures for identification and quantification of baseline emissions and/or removals that would 
have occurred in the absence of the activities involving the REDD project component is selected with 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
129 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.3 
reference to the decision tree provided in Table 1 of VM0007 (v1.7) and considered in combination 
with various modules applicable for tidal wetland areas as provided in Table 3 and Table 4 in VM0007. 
 
Applying the above identified methodology and applicable tools for baseline emission estimates for 
expected  unplanned  deforestation  and  degradation,  the  following  equations  are  applied  in  the 
sequence provided below for completing the estimates. The keys aspects of the estimations completed 
are explained with formulas that are applied for completing the estimates with details included in the 
associated tool of VM0007 which is VMD0007 (v3.3). 
 
Step  4.3  of  VMD0007:  Estimation  of  the  sum  of  baseline  carbon  stock  changes  (terrestrial 
carbon stock) 
• Equation (23): Area of unplanned deforestation in forest stratum 
• Equations  (23),  (15)  and  (16),  and  Module  CP-AB  (Part  1)  and  Part  (3):  Baseline  carbon  stock 
change in AGB 
• Equation (23): Carbon stock entering the wood products pool 
• Equations (23) and (20): Baseline carbon stock change in litter 
• Equations (23), (17) and (18) and Module CP-AB (Part 3): Baseline carbon stock change in BGB 
• Equations (23) and (19): Baseline carbon stock change in deadwood. 
 
Step 4.4 of VMD0007: Estimation of baseline greenhouse gas emissions from wetlands SOC 
pool 
• Equation (5) of VMD0051 (v1.0) or BL-TW: SOC stock in in-situ tidal wetland soil material 
• Equation (5) of BL-TW: CO2 emissions from in-situ tidal wetland SOC pool 
• Equation (22) of BL-TW: SOC stock in eroded tidal wetland soil material 
• Equation  (25)  of  BL-TW: SOC loss due to oxidation as a % of ‘C’ mass present in eroded tidal 
wetland soil material 
• Equation (4) of BL-TW: CO2 emissions from tidal wetland SOC pool 
• Equations (33) and (34) of BL-TW: CH4 emissions from tidal wetland SOC pool 
• Equations (36) and (37) of BL-TW: N2O emissions from tidal wetland SOC pool 
 
Applying the above, the Total Baseline Emissions from Degradation is estimated 
• Equation (2) of BL-TW: Net GHG emissions in the WRC baseline scenario.

stratum. The baseline carbon stock change in the AGB is calculated as follows:

The area of unplanned deforestation (Aunplanned,i,t) in both forest strata, i.e., ‘Mangrove Forest 
stratum’ and ‘Swamp Forest stratum’ in year ‘t’ are calculated by identifying suitable reference region 
and estimating historical deforestation rates, using the procedures outlined in VMD0007 (BL-UP) for 
a  reference  period  of  10  years  (2013 – 2022).  This  was  completed  by  analyzing  remotely  sensed 
historical  data  for identification of  comparable  reference  region  areas within Indonesia applying the 
methods for identifying and estimating the ‘Reference region for projecting rate of deforestation’ as 
per section 1.1.1.1 of Part 1 of BL-UP and estimating ‘Annual areas of unplanned deforestation’ as 
per Steps 2.1, 2.2 and 2.3 of Part 2 of BL-UP. Location analysis for deforestation is not required due 
to the ‘mosaic configuration’ of deforestation as explained in Step 3.0 of Part 2 of BL-UP. The results 
for the ‘Reference Region of Deforestation (“RRD”)’ analysis are included in Table 53 for the two 
dominant forest strata kin the project area.

VMD0050 (version 1.0) or (BL-TW) is applied to estimate CO2e emissions in the baseline that will not 
be emitted as a result of implementation of the project activity which is part of a tidal ecosystem. This 
is applied only to the area where REDD project activities are implemented.

section  5.3.6.4  of  VMD0050).  The  N2O  emissions  are  estimated  as  follows,  considering  that  the

Applying the procedures explained above, the total baseline emissions in the baseline scenario for the 
REDD  component  in  the  project  is  estimated  for  the  30-years  crediting  period  on  ex-ante  basis.

two succeeding 10-year periods. The baseline for the SOC pool is estimated for 20 years (refer Step 
4.3 at page 33 of VMD0007).

3.2.2 Project Emissions (VCS, 3.15) 
IFM  component:  During  planning,  implementation  and  operation  activities, GHG  emissions  may 
occur.  In  addition,  natural events  like  forest fires may  occur.  These  are listed below  as  possible 
sources of project emissions: 
 
a. administration and Planning (Electricity and Fuel Consumption) (E
projplan,t
), 
b. travel for design and set up (e.g., consultation and education) (fuel consumption) (E
design,t
), 
c. travel for implementing monitoring plan (e.g., from on-the-ground forest surveillance) (E
monitoring,t
), 
and 
d. Natural disturbances such as forest fires (C
natdisturb,t
).

The  three  components  of  the  project  activity  will  be  implemented  and  operated  applying  common 
resources and utilities. Being part of a combined project that includes ARR and REDD activities, the 
above potential sources of project emissions are estimated on a combined basis for all three types of 
project activity components. These project emission components, namely, IFM, ARR and REDD, can 
be summed up using the following equation: 
 
Equation 4-1 (to be modified to exclude Cillegal_harvest,t) from VM0011:

components,  except  for those  project  emissions  mentioned  below  are not  included  in  Equation  4-1 
above but will be included in the ex post estimation of the project emissions during the crediting period.

CIW+REDD component: Methods for estimating net carbon stock changes and GHG emissions in 
the project scenario are provided in Module M-REDD. The net GHG emissions in the project scenario, 
as  per Equation  (1) in  Module  M-REDD,  should  be  estimated  as  the  sum  of  stock  changes  due  to 
deforestation  and  forest  degradation  plus  the  total  GHG  emissions  minus  any  eligible  forest  stock 
enhancements. In this project, the monitoring and estimation of the above parameters are addressed 
as below for each of the two forest strata which are ‘Mangrove Forest stratum’ and ‘Swamp Forest 
stratum’. 
 
• Net carbon stock change as a result of deforestation in the project area in the project case 
in stratum ‘I’ in year ‘t’: the aim of this REDD project is to totally stop any deforestation that has 
been occurring anywhere in the project area prior to implementation of the project activity, and fully 
prevent any that would have occurred in the absence of this project activity. The performance will 
be  monitoring,  and  If  any  event  occurs,  this  type  of  project  emissions  will  be  monitored  and 
accounted using the same approach explained as C
illegal_harvest,t
 for the IFM component. Hence, for 
both ex ante and ex-post periods, no deforestation is anticipated and included in project emissions. 
 
• Net carbon stock change as a result of degradation in the project area in the project case in 
stratum ‘i’ in year ‘t’: since no deforestation is expected as described above, no project emission 
from degradation is anticipated. 
 
• Net carbon stock change as a result of natural disturbance in the project area in the project 
case in stratum ‘i’ in year ‘t’: If any event occurs, this type of project emissions will be monitored 
and accounted as part of C
natdisturb,t
 for the IFM component. 
 
• Greenhouse gas emissions as a result of deforestation and degradation activities within the 
project area in the project case in stratum ‘i’ in year ‘t’: this  is  generally  not  applicable  as 
explained above for ‘net carbon stock changes as a result of deforestation and degradation’. 
 
• Net carbon stock change as a result of forest growth and sequestration during the project 
baseline in areas projected to be deforested in the in stratum ‘i’ in year ‘t’: on a conservative 
basis, no benefits will be included for these parameters and is excluded. 
 
The above information is not available at the time of completing this PD and will be monitored prior to 
each monitoring event. Hence, for ex ante estimation of project emissions, the total project emissions 
comprising  all  three  project  components  is  assumed  as  0.15%  of  baseline  emissions  for  the  IFM 
component.  However,  the  actuals  project  emissions  for the  entire  project  comprising all  three 
components  will  be  calculated  ex  post  during  each  monitoring  event  by  applying  Equation  4-1 
explained above on a combined basis inclusive of the ARR and REDD components. 
3.2.3 Leakage Emissions (VCS 2.5, 3.2, 3.6, 3.15, 4.3) 
IFM component: As per VM0011, three potential sources of leakage could increase GHG emissions 
outside a project’s boundary. Each of these sources is assessed below to identify if any is relevant or 
expected to be significant in the IFM component of this project. 

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
141 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.3 
 
1. Carbon losses from degradation due to baseline activity shifting in other lands managed or 
operated by the Project Proponent: While implementing this project, the Project Proponents have 
clearly communicated not to pursue any further timbering activity within or outside the project area, 
and instead transform its business model to conservation of eco-systems in the project area should 
carbon finance from sale of carbon offsets from VCS registration of the IFM (and associated ARR 
and REDD) project is available. Therefore, carbon losses as a result of degradation are not relevant 
to the IFM component of this project. 
 
2. Carbon  emissions  from  implementation  of  shifted  timber logging  activities  in  other  lands 
managed or operated by the Project Proponent: With reference to explanation provided above 
for ‘Carbon losses from degradation’, this type of carbon emissions is not applicable to the IFM 
component of this project. 
 
3. Carbon  from  market  leakage  due  to  shifts  in  supply  and  demand  of  the  products  and 
services  affected  by  the  project  activity:  Market  effects  as  a  result  of an IFM  project  could 
potentially occur  due to  (1)  intensification  of  existing  harvest  practices  and  (2)  formation  of  new 
enterprises  and  hence, the Project  Proponents have  clearly  communicated  not  to  pursue  any 
further new (or modified existing) FIRs for sanctioned selective logging. In the IFM component of 
this project, the former event did not and is not expected to occur due to reducing scale of timber 
logging  until  full  discontinuation  by  the Project  Proponents (new  owners/management  of  the 
concession area) in the past five years prior to start of the project activity (where, 'Actual Harvesting 
Volume' < 'Historical Harvesting Volume before 5years' < ‘RKU approved merchantable volume’). 
The latter event is also not expected due to low to final discontinuation of timber logging. Therefore, 
carbon losses as a result of market leakage are not significant if could occur at all due to the IFM 
component of this project. 
 
Also to be noted, as per VM0011 (section 1.2.1), ‘the ex ante estimation for leakage assessment will 
be zero’. 
 
ARR component: With reference to section 8.2.2 of VM0047, leakage emissions in ARR projects the 
implementation of the project activities does not involve burning of biomass or use of any nitrogenous 
fertilisers. Hence, no GHG leakage is expected as a result of the ARR component of this project. 
 
CIW+REDD  component:  As  per  VM0011  and  Module  BL-UP  (section  1.1),  leakage  belt  is  not 
mandatory for inclusion if 100% of the project area was forested at the start of the project, which is 
true in this case. As per Module BL-UP (section 1.1.3) and Module LK-ASU (section 5.1.1), leakage is 
to  be  included  if  the  REDD  project  displaces  unplanned  deforestation  and  degradation  to  other 
locations  by  (1)  Local  Deforestation  Agents  and  (2)  Immigrant  Deforestation  Agents.  There  are  no 
resident  populations  with  2km  radius  of  the  project  area  and  any  leakage  belt  where  unplanned 
deforestation  can  shift.  The  likely  number  of  individuals  who  could  be  considered  as  Local 
Deforestation Agents is limited and to be provided with employment in the project for forest patrolling 
as alternate livelihood which is a more sustainable occupation. This measure in the project design also 
eliminates any possibility of leakage from market effects within 50 km of the project (refer Module LK-

   CCB & VCS Project Description Template  
                                                                                                CCB Version 3.0, VCS Version 4.4 
142 
CCB v3.0, VCS v4.3 
ME). Therefore, no leakage as a result of implementation of the REDD component of the project is 
expected. 
 
Overall considering the entire VCS project comprising all three components (IFM, ARR and REDD), 
no changes to hydrological connectivity is expected as a result of implementation of the project that 
may  alter the  mean  annual  water table  depths or flooding  frequency  or duration  in  and  around  the 
project  area.  Therefore,  no  GHG  emission  increase  is  expected  to  occur  of  the  types  described  in 
module LK-ECO for emissions from ecological leakage. 
3.2.4 Estimated GHG Emission Reductions and Carbon Dioxide Removals (VCS, 3.15, 4.1) 
The net anthropogenic GHG emission reductions and removals for this project result from those for 
the  three  individual  components  (IFM,  ARR  and  REDD),  each  of  which  is  explained  below taking 
reference to the equations and formulas applied. 
 
IFM  component:  As  per VM0011  (section  1.2.1),  the  net  anthropogenic  GHG  emission  reductions 
(C’
IFM-LtPF,t
)  for  time  period ‘t’ is calculated by subtracting emissions associated with project activity 
(C’
actual,t
)  and  leakage  (C’
leakage,t
)  from  carbon  emissions  associated  with  the  baseline  scenario 
(C’

). 
 
Equation 1-1

 = C’

 - C’

The uncertainty assessment for C’

 is a cumulative uncertainty assessment for all parameters 
used  for  its  estimation.  This  assessment  is  completed  with  reference  to  section  6  in  VM0011  as 
described below. The uncertainty assessments for the individual input parameters that are estimated 
based  on  ex  ante  field  measurements  in  representative  sampling  plots  were  also  completed. The 
generic functions for formulas applied for calculations leading to the estimation of C’
IFM-LtPF,t
 are of the 
nature ‘z = x + y’ and ‘fn = x * y * y’. 
 
The uncertainties for both types of these functions are assessed by applying the following two rules, 
respectively. 
 
Rule 1 for ‘z = x + y’:  σ

 = √ (σ
y
2

z
2
) 
 
Rule 2 for ‘fn = x * y * y’:  σ

}

}

where, the terms σ

The relative error or percentage error for a function ‘fn’ is represented by: 
 
U

fn

The uncertainty assessment for Carbon dioxide removals due to ARR refers to VM0047 (section 8.4). 
Uncertainty  in  parameter  N,  population  size,  is  assumed  to  be  zero  and is  addressed  via  the 
requirement  for  complete  census  of  planting  units.  The  project  method  baseline,  equal  to  zero 
(absence of planting units), is assumed to have zero uncertainty.

3.3.3 Monitoring Plan (VCS, 3.16, 3.20) 
The project has a detailed monitoring plan that will mostly be implemented by the project field team. 
Each field team personnel responsible for specific functions in the project are provided with adequate 
equipment, training, and ‘standard operating procedures (“SOPs”)’ to carry out the planned monitoring. 
All monitoring information will be evaluated and archived in both physical and electronic formats, for 
the  purposes  of  project  operations  and  performance management,  and  for  estimating  the  GHG 
removals and avoidance achieved.

The monitoring  of  various  parameters ex  post  and  during  the  crediting  period  and  their  use  for the 
annual estimation of project performance and actual emission reductions will be based on SOPs and 
work instructions  developed  by  the Project  Proponents. These could be  verified  by  the VVB  during 
project validation. The following aspects are included and refer to the data and parameters set out in 
Section 3.3.2 (Data and Parameters Monitored): 
 
• Carbon stocks changes 
• Land cover changes 
• Tree diameter increment 
• Other climate parameters such as incidents of any forest fire. 
 
The Project Proponent has developed procedures for: 
 
- measuring, recording, storing, aggregating, collating and reporting data and parameters; 
 
- monitoring roles/responsibilities for designated staff in the project team; 
 
- QA/QC  to  verify  the  accuracy  and  representativeness  of  the  monitored  data  including  any 
sampling processes applied; and 
 
- handling any non-conformances with the validated monitoring plan. 
 
Internal audit will  be  carried  out  annually  to  check  the  conformity  of  fieldwork  and  documents  in 
accordance with the Verra requirements prior to completion of monitoring report for VCU verification 
events. 
3.3.4 Dissemination of Monitoring Plan and Results (VCS, 3.18; CCB, CL4.2) 
The Project Proponents will use possibly three methods of communications with various stakeholders 
for disseminating project related information and aiming to guarantee access to documents including 
monitoring plan on a need-to-know basis.  
1. Writing,  a  printed  version  of  each  document  related  to  the  project,  such  as  the  project 
description,  monitoring  report,  validation  and  verification  report  and  the  summary  will  be 
available for consultation at Project Conservation office both headquarter and field office. 
2. Information and news related to the project will also be conveyed through village office.  
3. Virtual document related to the project are available through project website.
